Jamison Brereton

135
Va╠Дyu (1тАУ3, 9), Indra and Va╠Дyu (4тАУ8)
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
9 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi, except aс╣гс╣нi 7тАУ8, arranged in tr╠еcas
The second of ParuchepaтАЩs V─Бyu hymns is longer than the first, and presumably originally consisted of three hymns, corresponding to the tr╠еca divisions. For most of its length it is preoccupied with the usual themes of V─Бyu hymns: V─БyuтАЩs journey to the sacrifice with his many teams and his right to the first drink of soma at the Morning Pressing. The first tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3) is an invitation to V─Бyu alone; the second (vss. 4тАУ6), thematically and verbally parallel to the first, is addressed to V─Бyu and Indra, who share the second soma oblation at the Morning Pressing.
The last tr╠еca (vss. 7тАУ9) is less straightforward. The first of its verses (7) seems to describes an ongoing sacrifice to which V─Бyu and Indra are traveling, a journey con tinued in the first part of verse 8. And the fortunate results of the successful sacri fice are described at the end of verse 8, the thriving of stock and agriculture. But in between is the mention of a mysterious fig tree. The final verse (9) is even more mys terious, with its unidentified oxen of paradoxical movement and habits. Since the vocabulary is reminiscent of the Marut lexicon, the oxen may be the Maruts, and the association of V─Бyu (Wind) with the thunderstorm may be depicted. The pas sage also reminds us of the mysterious oxen in I.105.10, which may be astronomical

phenomena. And, of course, in a hymn focused on the soma sacrifice, any unidenti fied referent may be the soma drinks.

English translation:

тАЬApproach our strewngrass, V─Бyu, with (your) thousand steeds, to partake of the (offered) food, (prepared) for the lord of the steeds; (approach) with hundreds (to the sacrifice prepared) for thelord of the steeds; the gods holdback for you as the deity (entitled) first to drink (Soma); the sweet effused (Soma) are ready for your exhilaration; are redy for their function.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The ritual grass is strewn. Drive up to us, to pursue it, with a thousandfold team, o teamsterтАФwith hundredfold (teams), o teamsterтАФ
for the gods have conceded to you, the god, to drink first.
The pressed, honeyed (soma drinks) have been set forth for youтАФhave been set forth for your exhilaration and for your resolve.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Unaccented niyutvate in bc appears to be a voc. to an otherwise unattested -istem niyutvati-, whose formation would be morphologically peculiar (a secondary -istem built to a -vant-stem?!). It must be a nonce manipulation of the standard -vantstem niy├║tvant-. As Renou points out, vocatives in -pate may have had some influence in producing this rhyme form. Since V─Бyu is almost the only referent of niy├║tvant-, it is highly unlikely that the form represents a dative to the -vant-stem that lost its accent for some reason.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFor you this Soma, purified by the stones (that bruise), and clothed with enviable (splendour), flows to its (appropriate) receptacle; clothed with brilliant (splendour), this Soma is offered as your portion amongst men and amongst gods; (having received it), harness your horses, and depart well effected towards us; gratified, and well disposed towards us, depart.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Parip┼лto adribhiс╕е = abhiс╣гava┼Ы─Бdhanair apagatarj─л┼Ыodhitaс╕е, purified by the impurity which has been removed by the purifying means of the effusion;

с╣Ъjiс╣гa = gatasaraс╕е soma, i.e. soma that has lost its strength; da┼Ы─Бpavitra┼Ыodhanena grahaс╣Зena v─Б ┼Ыodhitaс╕е = purified by straining through ku┼Ыa grass, or by taking hold of; sp─Бrh─Б vas─Бnaс╕е = sprhaс╣З─лy─Бni tej─Бс╣Гsi pidh─Бnaс╕е, putting on desirable or enviable splendours; pari ko┼Ыam arс╣гati = ko┼Ыa-sth─Бn─лyam grahampr─Бpnoti, it goes to the ladle, as it were, in plural ce of a receptacle

Jamison Brereton

For you has this soma been purified all around by the stones; clothing himself in coveted (garments) he rushes around the caskтАФclothing
himself in gleaming (garments) he rushes.
For you is this portion poured among the ─Аyus, is the soma poured among the gods.
Travel, V─Бyu; drive to our teams [=poetic thoughts], seeking usтАФdrive at your pleasure, seeking us.

Griffith

Purified by the stones the Soma flows for thee, clothed with its lovely splendours, to the reservoir, flows clad in its refulgent light.
For thee the Soma is poured forth, thy portioned share mid Gods and men.
Drive thou thy horses, Vayu, come to us with love, come well-inclined and loving us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome with hundreds and thousand of your steeds to our sacrifice to partake of (the sacrificial) food; (come), V─Бyu, to partake of the oblations; this is your reasonable portion, and it is radiant along with the sun; the Soma (portions) borne by the priests are prepared; the pure Soma (portions), V─Бyu, are prepared.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With your hundredfold teams drive here to our ceremony, with
thousandfold ones to pursue itтАФo V─Бyu, to pursue our oblations.
Yours is this portion at its proper time, accompanying the reins [=rays] when the sun (rises).
Being carried, they have been guided by the AdhvaryusтАФo V─Бyu, the gleaming (soma drinks) have been guided.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this hymn is divided into tс╣Ыcas and each tс╣Ыca was probably originally a single hymn. This then is the final verse of 1-3, and it exhibits very heavy ring-composition: 3b тАж ├║pa y─Бhi v─лt├бye reprises 1a ├║pa no y─Бhi v─лt├бye almost exactly, and 3ab тАж niy├║dbhiс╕е ┼Ыat├нnibhiс╕е тАж sahasr├нnibhiс╕е тАж echoes 1bc sah├бsreс╣Зa niy├║t─Б тАж ┼Ыat├нn─лbhiс╕е. Note also 3d t├бv─Бy├бm bh─Бg├бс╕е тАж, which is identical to the beginning of 2d.

As discussed ad I.134.3, the expression here, s├бra┼Ыmiс╕е s┼л╠Бrye s├бc─Б тАЬaccompanying the reins [=rays] when the sun (rises)тАЭ seems to me a fuller version of the temporal expression ra┼Ыm├нс╣гu (/ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е) тАЬat/with the reins=rays.тАЭ See also I.137.2e s─Бk├бс╣Г s┼л╠Бryasya ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е тАЬsimultaneous with the reins=rays of the sun.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fronted forms of tv├бm (etc.) found in I.134.4-6 continue here, though not as densely: 1d, 2a, d, 3d.

Griffith

Come thou with hundreds, come with thousands in thy team to this our solemn rite, to taste the sacred food, Vayu, to taste the offerings.
This is thy seasonable share, that comes co-radiant with the Sun.
Brought by attendant priests pure juice is offered up, Vayu, pure juice is offered up.

Geldner

Komm mit den hundertfachen Niyut-Gespannen zu unserem Opfer, mit den tausendfachen um zu genie├Яen, o Vayu, um die Opfergaben zu genie├Яen!Dies ist dein zeitgem├д├Яer Anteil, der bei aufgehender Sonne bestrahlte. Von den Adhvaryu┬┤s aufgetragen sind sie dargereicht, sind die klaren Somatr├дnke dargereicht, o Vayu.

Grassmann

Mit hundertfachen Rossescharen komme her zum Opferfest, mit tausendfachen zu dem Mahl, o Vaju, zu dem Opfermahl; Hier ist der Theil der dir geb├╝hrt, der Sonne gleich an hellem Licht, Die hellen Tr├дnke, von den Dienern dargebracht, die hellen sind dir dargereicht.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдмрд▓ рд╕реЗ рдЪреМрдЧреБрдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ рдмрд▓ рдХрд░ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдпреБрджреНрдз рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдФрд░ рд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╡рд░реНрд╖ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЬрд┐рддрдирд╛ рдХрд░ рд▓реЗрдирд╛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛ рдЙрддрдирд╛ рд╣реА рд▓реЗрд╡реЗрдВ рддрдерд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреА рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее рей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ рддрд╡ рдпреЗрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрднрд┐рд░реНрднрд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛ рдЬрдирд╛ рдЕрдпрдВрд╕рдд рддреЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдордпрдВрд╕рдд рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╡ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗ рд╕рдЪрд╛ рд╢реБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╕рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рд░реНрдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬреЛрд╜рдпрдВ рднрд╛рдЧреЛрд╜рд╕реНрддрд┐ рд╕ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрдпреБрдкрдпрд╛рд╣рд┐ рд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ рдпреЗ рд╢рддрд┐рдиреАрднрд┐рд╕реНрд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд┐рдгреАрднрд┐рд░реНрдирд┐рдпреБрджреНрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡реАрддрдпреЗ рдиреЛрд╜рдзреНрд╡рд░рдореБрдкрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореБрдкрд╛рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐ рее рей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднреНрдпрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдирд┐рдпреБрджреНрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдЧреБрдгрд╡рджреНрд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреИрд░рд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ (рд╢рддрд┐рдиреАрднрд┐рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдореВрднрд┐рдГ (рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░рдореН) рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореН (рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд┐рдгреАрднрд┐рдГ) рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╕рдВрдШрд╛ рдпрд╛рд╕реБ рддрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рдЙрдк) (рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) (рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛рдпреИ (рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рд╣рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐) рдЖрджрд╛рддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рд╛рдгрд┐ (рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдпреЗ (рддрд╡) (рдЕрдпрдореН) (рднрд╛рдЧрдГ) (рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдпрдГ) рдЛрддреБрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдп рд╕ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдпрдГ (рд╕рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдГ) рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реИрдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЗ) (рд╕рдЪрд╛) рд╕рдорд╡реЗрддрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрднрд┐рдГ) рдп рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдордзреНрд╡рд░рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреИрдГ (рднрд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ) рдзрд░рдорд╛рдгрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдпрдВрд╕рдд) рдЙрдкрдпрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдпреБрдГ (рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╢реБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╢реБрджреНрдзрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдпрдВрд╕рдд) рее рей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

English translation:

тАЬLet the chariot drawn by the Niyuts convey you both, (Indra and V─Бyu, to the sacrifice), for our preservation, and to partake of the consecrated viands; to partake, V─Бyu, of the oblations; drink of the sweet beverage;for the first draught is your (joing) due. V─Бyu (and Indra), come with joy-bestowing wealth; Indra (and V─Бyu), come with wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Precedence is given to V─Бyu; V─Бyav─Бgatam, nominative is in the singular and the verb in the dual; indra┼Ыca-─Бgatam, implying therefore, that one of the two is understood

Jamison Brereton

The chariot with its team will convey you two here for aid, to pursue the well-placed pleasurable offeringsтАФo V─Бyu, to pursue the oblations.
Drink of the honey of the stalk, for the first drinking was established for you two.
O V─Бyu, you two come here with shimmering bountyтАФand Indra, you two come here with bounty.

The v─Б╠Бyav ├нndra┼Ы ca construction here unfolds over two p─Бdas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is constructed in parallel to 1-3, but addressed to the two gods V─Бyu and Indra rather than V─Бyu alone. I will not call attention to the pervasively parallel phraseology: a simple skimming of the two sets of verses will amply demonstrate it.

Griffith

The chariot with its team of horses bring you both, to guard us and to taste the well-appointed food, Vayu, to taste the offerings!
Drink of the pleasant-flavoured juice: the first draught is assigned to you.
O Vayu, with your splendid bounty come ye both, Indra, with bounty come ye both.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe pious acts (addressed) to you have given augmented (efficacy) to our sacrifices; for you, (the priests) strain this quick-dropping Soma, as (the grooms rub down) a fleet, quick-running courser; drink of their (libations), and come hither, well disposed towards us, for our protection; do you both drink of the Soma that have been expressed by the stones, for you are both givers of food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As the grooms rub down: the intended verb is: marmс╣Ыjanta, have strained or cleaned, or rubbed; v─Бjinam, ─Б┼Ыumatyam na v─Бjinam = lit. going quick, like a quick horse, going quick

Jamison Brereton

Our thoughts should turn you two hither to our ceremonies; they keep grooming this drop, the prizewinnerтАФ(the drop) swift like a
prizewinning steed.
Drink of these (soma drinks), seeking us; come here to us with help. O Indra and V─Бyu, (drink) of them, pressed by stones, you twoтАФ(drink) to exhilaration, you two prize-givers. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is constructed in parallel to 1-3, but addressed to the two gods V─Бyu and Indra rather than V─Бyu alone. I will not call attention to the pervasively parallel phraseology: a simple skimming of the two sets of verses will amply demonstrate it.

Griffith

May our songs bring you hither to our solemn rites: these drops of mighty vigour have they beautified, like a swift steed of mighty strength.
Drink of them well-inclined to us, come hitherward to be our help.
Drink, Indra-Vayu, of these Juices pressed with stones, Strength-givers! till they gladden you.

Geldner

Euch sollen die Gebete herbringen zu den Opfern. Sie putzen diesen Saft, der den Preis gewinnt, wie ein schnelles Ro├Я, das den Preis gewinnt. Trinkt davon, uns geneigt - kommt hierher zu uns mit Gunst - Indra und Vayu, trinkt von dem mit Steinen ausgepre├Яten Soma, ihr Geber des Siegerpreises, zum Rausch!

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese Soma, poured out in our rites, and borne by the priests, are prepared for you both; the pure Soma, V─Бyu (and Indra), are prepared; these pervading (effusions) have passed through the oblique filter for you both; the Soma intended for you both, pass through the woolly fleece; the inexhaustible soma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abhyasс╣Ыkс╣гata tiraс╕е pavitram: pavitram is a term applied to bundle of ku┼Ыa grass, which is supposed to purify the Soma or the butter poured upon it; it is here explained the receiver of the Soma plural ced slopingly or obliquely, or a filter or a strainer made of wool. atirom─Бс╣Зyavyay─Б som─Бso atyavyay─Б: Soma having gone through (ati) the unclipped (avyay─Бni for acchinn─Бni) hairs; or, avyaya = avimay─Бni, made from the sheep, sheep’s wool; fall into the vessel that receives them; in the second occurrence, avyay─Б = unexpended, unexhausted

Jamison Brereton

These soma drinks were pressed here in the waters for you two. Being carried, they have been guided by the AdhvaryusтАФo V─Бyu, the
gleaming (soma drinks) have been guided.
They have surged toward you two, swift across the filter,
seeking you two beyond the sheepтАЩs fleeceтАФthe soma drinks beyond the sheepтАЩs (fleece). с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
04-06 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, this tс╣Ыca is constructed in parallel to 1-3, but addressed to the two gods V─Бyu and Indra rather than V─Бyu alone. I will not call attention to the pervasively parallel phraseology: a simple skimming of the two sets of verses will amply demonstrate it.

Griffith

These Soma juices pressed for you in waters here, borne by attendant priests, are offered up to you: bright, Vayu, are they offered up.
Swift through the strainer have they flowed, and here are shed for both of you,
Soma-drops, fain for you, over the wether’s fleece, Somas over the wether’s fleece.

Geldner

F├╝r euch beide sind diese Somatr├дnke hier ins Wasser ausgepre├Яt. Von den Adhvaryu┬┤s aufgetragen sind sie dargereicht, sind die klaren dir, Vayu, dargereicht. Diese sind f├╝r euch beide durch die Seihe gesprengt wie rasche Rosse, nach euch verlangend durch die Schafhaare, die Somatr├дnke durch die Schafhaare.

Grassmann

Im Wasser sind die Soma’s hier euch ausgepresst, gebracht von Dienern sind sie hier euch dargereicht, die hellen, Vaju, dargereicht; Euch beiden sind ergossen sie, die schnellen durch die Seihe hier; Zu euch hindringend durch der Widderwolle Sieb die Soma’s durch das Widderfell.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPass, (V─Бyu), by the many sleeping (worshippers) and go (with Indra) to the house where the stone resounds; Indra (and V─Бyu), go to that dwelling; (go where) the (word of) truth is manifest; (go where) the butter flows; go both well-fed horses to the sacrifice; Indra (and V─Бyu), repair to the sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O V─Бyu, drive beyond sleeper after sleeper. Where the pressing stone speaks, you two go thereтАФ(you) and Indra, go to that house.
Liberality has been sighted; the ghee is flowing. With a full team you two drive to the ceremonyтАФ(you) and Indra drive to the ceremony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the v─Б╠Бyav ├нndra┼Ы ca construction is stretched from a to c, and in f the sequence ├нndra┼Ы ca y─Бthaс╕е (lit. тАЬand Indra, you two driveтАЭ) presupposes a 2nd ps. sg.

to produce the conjoined subject. This latter construction further attenuates the v─Б╠Бyav ├нndra┼Ы ca construction.

Note the little figure sasat├│ тАж ┼Ы├б┼Ыvato.

Griffith

O Vayu, pass thou over all the slumberers, and where the press-stone rings enter ye both that house, yea, Indra, go ye both within.
The joyous Maiden is beheld, the butter flows. With richly laden team come to our solemn rite, yea, Indra, come ye to the rite.

Geldner

An allen Schl├дfern geh vor├╝ber, Vayu! Wo der Stein ert├╢nt, dorthin kommt, du und Indra, kommt ins Haus! Die Gro├Яmut lie├Я sich sehen, das Schmalz flie├Яt. Ihr fahret mit vollz├дhligem Gespann zum Opfer; du und Indra, ihr fahret zum Opfer.

Grassmann

O Vaju schreite ├╝ber alle Schlafenden, wo t├╢nt der Pressstein, dahin kommet in das Haus, dahin, o Indra, Vaju, kommt; Wo lieblich scheint der Morgen und die Butter fliesst, zum Opfer kommt mit reichgef├╝lltem Wagenzug, zum Opfer Indra, Vaju ihr.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThen, accept the libations of the sweet Soma at the sacrifice in which the triumphant priests stand round the rock-born (plural nt); may they ever be victorious for us; (for you) together the cows distil (their milk); the (offering of) barley is dressed; and never for you, (V─Бyu), will the cows grow meagre. never will the kine be carried off (by thieves).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A┼Ыvattham upatiс╣гс╣нhanti: a┼Ыvattha = the religious fig tree; explained here as the Soma found spread through mountains and the like, parvat─Бdi vy─Бtiprade┼Ыe sthitam; na upadasyanti dhenavaс╕е-n─Бpa dasyanti dhenavaс╕е: upadas = infirm, or wasted by sickness;

Apadas = to be carried off by thieves

Jamison Brereton

Just now you two travel to the poured offering of honey. The victorious ones [=soma drinks? Maruts?] that approach the fig treeтАФlet these be victorious for us.
All at once the cows give birth and the grain ripens; the milk-cows do not give out for you, o V─БyuтАФthe milk-cows do not give up.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As indicated in the published introduction, I have no idea what the figtree represents here. Some of the verse seems anagrammatic for v─Бy├║-: the repeated j─Бy├бvo (bc) and y├бvo (d).

The accent on s├║vate in d must result from juxtaposition with p├бcyate.

Griffith

Ride hither to the offering of the pleasant juice, the holy Fig-tree which victorious priests surround: victorious be they still for us.
At once the cows yield milk, the barley-meal is dressed. For thee,
O Vayu, never shall the cows grow thin, never for thee shall they be dry.

Geldner

Zu diesem fahret ihr nun, zu der Opferung des S├╝├Яtranks. Die unter den Asvattha-Baum als Sieger traten, die Sieger sollen bei uns sein. Mit einem Male geb├дren die K├╝he, reift das Korn. Nicht versiegen deine Milchk├╝he, o Vayu, nicht versiegen deine Milchk├╝he.

Grassmann

Ihr fahrt ja hin zu dieses Opfertranks Erguss zum Feigenholz, in dem die Tr├дnke kr├дftig stehn; bei uns auch seien kr├дftig sie; Die K├╝h’ geb├дren und die Gerste reift zugleich; nie geht, o Vaju, dir die Milch der K├╝he aus, die Milch versieget nimmer dir.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрддреНрд░) (рдЕрд╣) рдХрд┐рд▓ (рддрддреН) (рд╡рд╣реЗрдереЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрдГ (рдордзреНрд╡рдГ) рдордзреБрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рдЖрд╣реБрддрд┐рдореН) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреНрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН (рдпрдореН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рддреНрдердореН) рдкрд┐рдкреНрдкрд▓рдорд┐рд╡ (рдЙрдкрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрдд) рдЙрдкрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддреБ (рдЬрд╛рдпрд╡рдГ) рдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рддреЗ) (рд╕рдиреНрддреБ) (рдЬрд╛рдпрд╡рдГ) рдЬреЗрддрд╛рд░рдГ рд╢реВрд░рд╛рдГ (рд╕рд╛рдХрдореН) рд╕рд╣ (рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ) рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ (рд╕реБрд╡рддреЗ) рдЧрд░реНрднрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдореБрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ (рдкрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ) рдкрд░рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╡реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ (рдпрд╡рдГ) рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╛рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╡рд╛рдпреЛ) рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╡рджреНрдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдЙрдк) (рджрд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐) рдХреНрд╖рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ) (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдЕрдк) (рджрд╕реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐) (рдзреЗрдирд╡рдГ) рд╡рд╛рдгреНрдпрдГ рее рео рее

рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рди рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рее реирел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese your horses, excellent V─Бyu, strong of limb, youthful and full of vigour, bear you through the space between heaven and earth; growing (are they) in bulk, and strong as oxen; they are not lost in the firmament, but hold on their speed, unretarded by reviling; difficult are they to be arrested as the beams of the sun; difficult are they to be arrested by force.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Unretarded by reviling: agiraukasaс╕е = lit. having no dweling by speech; i.e. they are not brought to a stop by abusive speech of the like, bhartsn─Бdin─Б sthitim alabham─Бn─Бс╕е; hastayor dur-niyantavaс╕е, difficult to be checked by both hands, or by physical force; they are not to be deterred by words, such as voс╕е voс╕е; or by pulling up the rains, from coming to the sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Here, o V─Бyu, are those oxen of yours [=soma drinks? Maruts?],
arm-strong, which fly in the riverтАФthe oxen that are greatly arrogantтАФ that are not swift though on dry land, yet are nimble in the mountains though their home is not there,
like the reins [=rays] of the sun difficult to hold backтАФdifficult for the hands to hold back.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The references here are also murky, but I am inclined to see the plural referents as both Maruts and soma drinks. In favor of the Maruts: 1) they are called b─Бhv-├▓jas -in VIII.20.6; 2) they are sometimes called ukс╣г├бn- (e.g., V.52.3); 3) the non-waning cows of 8ef are also found in the Marut hymn V.55.5 n├б vo dasr─Б ├║pa dasyanti dhen├бvaс╕е; 4) they fly (e.g. V.59.7), and they’re associated with the shaking of mountains and the flowing of rivers (flying in the river could be rain); 5) approaching the figtree in 8b might be like V.54.12, where they тАЬshake the gleaming berry (p├нppalam)тАЭ – the pippala is supposed to be a fig.

nad─л╠Бis one of the rare loc. sg.s to a vс╣Ыk─л╠Б-fem.; see saras─л╠Бin VIII.103.2, gaur─л╠Б in IX.12.3, and AiG III.170.

Griffith

These Bulls of thine, O Vayu with the arm of strength, who swiftly fly within the current of thy stream, the Bulls increasing in their might,
Horseless, yet even through the waste swift-moving, whom no shout can stay,
Hard to be checked are they, like sunbeams, in their course. hard to be checked by both the hands.

Geldner

Diese sind fein deine beinstarken Stiere, o Vayu, die im Flusse fliegen, die m├дchtig sich reckenden Stiere, die auch im Steppenlande nicht schnell, und doch im Gebirge gar flink sind, obwohl im Gebirge nicht zu Hause, die schwer zu regieren sind wie die Z├╝gel der Sonne, in den H├дnden schwer zu regieren.

Grassmann

Die Helden stark an Armen, die du, Vaju, hast, die zwischen beiden Weltenstr├╢men fliegen hin, die Helden gross und stark an Kraft, Die ohne Rosse eilen doch in schneller Fahrt und ohne Rast, Sie sind unhemmbar wie der Sonne Strahlen stets, man hemmt sie mit den H├дnden nicht.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реИрд░реНрдмрд╛рд╣реБрдмрд▓рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░рдзреГрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреАрдпрд╛ рдпреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкрдГ рд╕рджрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрджреНрдзреЗрддреЗрддрд┐ рее реп реердЕрддреНрд░ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЛрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдиреА рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рди рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрдирд╛ рди рдШрд╛рдмрд░рдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рд╡реАрд░ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рд╕реЗрдиреЗрдд рдмрд╛рд│рдЧрд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╡рд╛рдвреЗрд▓. рее реп рее
